## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics ŌĆö nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear second-order oscillators. Common models include restoring forces depending on x (linear or nonlinear), damping depending on v (linear or nonlinear), and optional time-dependent forcing/parametric excitation via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Free particle / constant acceleration: dv_dt = c0 (baseline kinematics or constant body force)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke-type restoring acceleration)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-type structure)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos settings)
- Simple pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (large-angle oscillations with damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - c2 * x**2) * v - c3 * x (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-excitation via negative damping at small |v|)
- Quadratic / turbulent drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (damping growing ~|v|v)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip style velocity-independent friction term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically appear as odd functions of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*sin(x), -c*x - c*x^3), reflecting symmetry about x=0 and implying energy storage in position.
- Linear viscous dissipation maps to a term -c*v; nonlinear dissipation often scales like -c*v*Abs(v) (quadratic drag) or -c*v**3 (high-speed damping).
- Self-excited/limit-cycle oscillations often require velocity-dependent damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c0 - c1*x**2)*v (Van der Pol) or (c0 - c1*v**2)*v (Rayleigh).
- Time-independent (autonomous) oscillators usually omit explicit t; explicit t terms (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) indicate external forcing or parametric modulation and can produce resonance bands.
- Nonlinear stiffness terms like -c*x**3 imply amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening/softening behavior), which is a hallmark of Duffing-type dynamics.
- Using sin(x) instead of x in the restoring term indicates large-angle pendulum physics; replacing sin(x) by x recovers the small-angle linear oscillator approximation.
- Dry friction introduces a discontinuity at v=0 via sign(v), which can create nonsmooth dynamics (stiction, stick-slip) unlike smooth viscous damping.
- Terms proportional to x*v (or x**2*v) can represent position-dependent damping/feedback (e.g., aerodynamic or active control), often breaking simple harmonic symmetry.
- If dv_dt contains only x-dependent terms (no v), the system is typically nondissipative; if v-dependent terms are present with negative sign, trajectories tend to spiral toward fixed points.
